## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with x as displacement and t as time, which is the standard setup for an equation of motion of an oscillator written as dv_dt = f(x,t). Nonlinear oscillators typically express dv_dt as a (possibly nonlinear) restoring force in x plus optional explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations about a stable equilibrium)
- Shifted equilibrium / biased spring: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) (equilibrium at x=c1 due to preload/offset)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness correction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear elasticity)
- Pendulum equation (exact sine restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (rotational oscillator with gravity-driven torque)
- Sine with higher-harmonic correction: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * sin(c3 * x) (effective periodic potential with anharmonics)
- Nonlinear potential gradient (generic): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (motion in an even polynomial potential V(x))
- External periodic forcing (additive drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3) (driven oscillator; drive independent of x)
- External periodic forcing with multiple tones: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (multi-frequency forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Parametric excitation with nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (parametric drive plus Duffing nonlinearity)
- Piecewise/impact-like restoring approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x (odd restoring force with amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Softening via bounded restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) (restoring force saturates at large |x|)
- Periodic potential (washboard): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 (tilted periodic potential / constant bias force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends on x but not t (suggests time-invariant potential energy; look for odd-in-x restoring terms like -x, -x-x**3, -sin(x)).
- Stability near equilibrium: a stable fixed point at x=0 typically has dv_dt ≈ -c * x for small x; deviations indicate nonlinear stiffness (x**3, x**5, sin).
- Hardening vs softening nonlinearity: positive cubic restoring magnitude (e.g., -x - c*x**3 with c>0) implies frequency increases with amplitude; opposite sign implies softening.
- Periodic-in-x restoring force: sin(c*x) (and harmonics) indicates motion in a periodic potential; useful when dv_dt is bounded and repeats with x.
- Bounded restoring at large displacement: tanh(c*x) or similar indicates force saturation/clipping at large |x| (e.g., magnetic/electrostatic limits or geometric constraints).
- External additive drive: terms purely in t (e.g., cos(c*t+c0)) indicate direct forcing; expect resonance-like behavior if combined with -c*x.
- Parametric modulation: stiffness multiplying x with a periodic-in-t factor (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) suggests Mathieu/parametric resonance mechanisms.
- Equilibrium shift/bias: constant or offset terms (e.g., x-c0 or +c0) imply a shifted equilibrium position or constant bias force (tilted potential).
- Symmetry cue: if dv_dt is approximately odd in x (dv_dt(x,t) ≈ -dv_dt(-x,t)), prefer odd restoring structures (x, x**3, sin) over even powers.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)

GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 77

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(x,t)=0.422619160916855\,\sin(t)\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\,e^{-|x|}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to produce **(i)** exactly one pure sinusoid in \(t\) with constant amplitude \(0.4226...\) and no other \(t\)-dependence, **(ii)** a linear-in-\(x\) term with coefficient \(-1.15357...\), and **(iii)** an \(x e^{-|x|}\) term with the *same* coefficient \(-1.15357...\). No other \(x\)-nonlinearities, logs, rationals, etc. Absolute value must remain exactly as \(|x|\) in the exponent with coefficient \(-1\).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether extra terms can be zeroed out and whether the remaining structure can be parameter-fit to the GT (including sine/cos phase shifts).

---

### 1.
\(c0\cos(c1+t)+c2x+c3x e^{c4|x|}+c5\sin(\cdot)\cos(\cdot)\).
- The product \(\sin(\cdot)\cos(\cdot)\) is not present in GT; set \(c5=0\).
- Then we can match time term by phase shift: choose \(c0=0.422619...\), \(c1=-\pi/2\) so \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\).
- Match \(x\): \(c2=-1.1535719...\).
- Match \(x e^{-|x|}\): need \(c4=-1\) and \(c3=-1.1535719...\).
Works. **Match possible.**

### 2.
Has extra \(c6 e^{c7 t}\cos(\cdot)\) term; set \(c6=0\). Remaining is cosine-in-\(t\) + \(x\) + \(x e^{c5|x|}\). Choose \(c1=1\) and phase \(c2=-\pi/2\) (or use cosine-to-sine identity), and set \(c5=-1\), \(c3,c4\) to the needed coefficients. **Match possible.**

### 3.
Extra \(c5 e^{c6 t}\cos(\cdot)\); set \(c5=0\). Remaining matches as in (1). **Match possible.**

### 4.
Extra \(c6 x\cos(\cdot)\) (time-dependent coefficient on \(x\)); GT has none. Only way is \(c6=0\). Then remaining matches (cos + \(x\) + \(x e^{c5|x|}\)). **Match possible.**

### 5.
Extra \(c5\cos(c6 x + c7\sin(\cdot))\) depends on \(x\) and \(t\) in a non-GT way; must set \(c5=0\). Remaining matches like (1). **Match possible.**

### 6.
Extra \(c6 x\sin(\cdot)\); set \(c6=0\). Remaining matches. **Match possible.**

### 7.
Extra \(c5\sin(c6 x+c7)\cos(\cdot)\); set \(c5=0\). Remaining matches. **Match possible.**

### 8.
Has \(c3\log(c4 x+1)\) which cannot appear in GT; must set \(c3=0\). Remaining: cosine + \(c5 x + c6 x e^{c7|x|}\). Choose cosine phase to become \(\sin t\), set \(c7=-1\), and coefficients to \(-1.15357...\). **Match possible.**

### 9.
Has extra \(c6\log(c7 e^{c8 x}+1)\) (nonlinear in \(x\)); must set \(c6=0\). Remaining matches. **Match possible.**

### 10.

### 11.

### 12.

### 13.

### 14.
Contains \(x|x|\) and \(\sin(\cdot)|x|^4\) terms; set \(c1=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then \(c0 x + c2\cos(\cdot)+ c8 x e^{c9|x|}\). Use cosine phase to make \(\sin t\), set \(c9=-1\), and choose \(c0=c8=-1.15357...\). **Match possible.**

### 15.

### 16.

### 17.

### 18.
Has both \(\cos(c1+t)\) and \(\sin(c3 t+c4)\). GT needs only one sinusoid. Set one coefficient to 0, e.g. \(c0=0\), and use the sine term with \(c3=1\) and phase \(c4=0\), amplitude \(c2=0.422619...\). Then match \(x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\) via \(c5,c6,c7=-1\). **Match possible.**

### 19.

### 20.

### 21.

### 22.

### 23.

Note that `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2) = cos(π/2 - t)`, so `c0*cos(c1 + t)` with `c1 = -π/2` gives `c0*cos(t - π/2) = c0*sin(t)`. Similarly, `c0*cos(c1*t + c2)` with `c1 = 1` gives `c0*cos(t + c2) = c0*sin(t)` when `c2 = -π/2`.

The GT basis functions are: **{x, x·exp(-|x|), sin(t)}**
